## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by current population size P and possibly time t, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics models (density dependence, Allee effects, harvesting, immigration, seasonal forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources; constant per-capita growth rate)
- Constant immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net source/sink independent of P)
- Logistic density dependence (quadratic crowding): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (self-limitation via intraspecific competition)
- Theta-logistic (generalized crowding exponent): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible curvature of density dependence)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (per-capita growth declines ~log with size; asymmetric approach to carrying capacity)
- Allee effect (weak/strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) (1 - c2 * P) (positive density dependence at low P, crowding at high P)
- Proportional harvesting (effort-based): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P (removal proportional to population)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 (fixed quota removal; risk of collapse at low P)
- Saturating harvest / predation-like removal: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P / (P + c3) (limited take rate at high P)
- Time-varying intrinsic rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (seasonal environment affecting births/deaths)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P - c4 * P**2 (seasonality plus crowding)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (c2 + c3 * sin(c4 * t + c5))) (resource capacity fluctuates with time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is proportional to P (straight line through origin when plotting dP_dt vs P), it suggests constant per-capita growth (exponential growth/decay).
- A negative curvature in dP_dt vs P and a clear zero-crossing at high P indicates density dependence; a dominant -P**2 term implies logistic-like crowding.
- If dP_dt becomes negative at low P (or crosses zero at a positive P), factors like (P - c) indicate Allee thresholds or critical population sizes.
- If per-capita growth (dP_dt / P) decreases approximately linearly with P, logistic forms fit; if it decreases roughly linearly with log(P), Gompertz-type log terms fit.
- An additive constant term in dP_dt (±c) indicates immigration/emigration independent of current population size.
- Removal terms proportional to P (−c*P) represent constant per-capita mortality/harvest effort; removal terms independent of P (−c) represent quotas or fixed losses.
- Rational loss terms like P/(P+c) indicate saturation (limited harvesting capacity, handling time, or capped removal rate).
- Sin(c*t + phase) or cos(c*t + phase) structure in dP_dt indicates seasonal forcing; interaction with P (multiplicative) implies environment modulates per-capita rates.
- If the equilibrium level of P drifts periodically in time, carrying-capacity modulation via denominators like (c0 + c1*sin(c2*t)) is a common mechanism.

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(t,P)=0.4866911314650416\,P^{1/3}+0.4866911314650416\,P\,e^{-0.08577402101126279\,t}.
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **exactly** a sum of (i) a pure \(P^{1/3}\) term with no \(t\)-dependence and (ii) a \(P\exp(kt)\) term with \(k=-0.08577...\), and **no other nonzero terms**.

### 1.
Has polynomial terms \(P^3,P^2,P\), a power term \(P*c3*(P*c4)^{c5}\) (a \(P^{c5+1}\) type), and \(P*exp(c8 t)\). Cannot produce \(P^{1/3}\) without also having an extra factor \(P\) (all power terms are at least linear in \(P\)). **No.**

### 2.
All terms are proportional to \(P\): \(P*c0*(P*c1)^{c2}\), \(P*c3*(P*c4)^{c5}\), \(P*c6*exp(c7 t)\), \(P*c8\). Cannot make a standalone \(P^{1/3}\) term (always at least \(P\cdot P^{c2}=P^{c2+1}\)). **No.**

### 3.
Same issue: first term is \(P^{c2+1}\), second is \(P\exp(\cdot)\), plus a sine-of-log term independent of \(P\) in a complicated way; cannot equal \(P^{1/3}\) for all \(P\). **No.**

### 4.
All added terms are proportional to \(P\) (or \(P\sin\)), so cannot create \(P^{1/3}\). **No.**

### 5.
Has \(P^{c2+1}\) and \(P\exp(\cdot)\) and an extra \(P^{c5} \exp(\cdot)\) term. Still no way to get pure \(P^{1/3}\) (unless \(c2=-2/3\) gives \(P^{1/3}\), but then it is multiplied by constants including \(c1^{c2}\) and still fine; however it is still of the form \(P*c0*(P*c1)^{c2}=c0*c1^{c2} P^{c2+1}\), so yes it *can* make \(P^{1/3}\) by choosing \(c2=-2/3\). But then the second term is \(P*c3*exp(c4 t)\) which can match the \(P e^{-0.0857 t}\) term. The third term \(P^{c5}c6 e^{c7 t}\) must vanish: set \(c6=0\). This seems promising—except GT’s first term has **no \(t\)**, and in candidate 5 the first term has no \(t\) either. So candidate 5 actually *can* match. Wait: check carefully: candidate 5 is  
\(P*c0*(P*c1)^{c2} + P*c3*exp(c4*t) + P^{c5}*c6*exp(c7*t)\).  
Set \(c2=-2/3\) gives \(P^{1/3}\). Set \(c6=0\) removes last term. Then choose \(c4=-0.0857740210...\), and choose \(c3=0.4866911314...\). For the first term, need \(c0*c1^{c2}=0.4866911314...\). Since \(c1\) is free and \(c2=-2/3\), pick e.g. \(c1=1\), \(c0=0.4866911314...\). This matches exactly.  
So **Yes, candidate 5 matches**.

(We still continue briefly to ensure no contradictions; but one match is enough.)
